    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText5967272852217032169" style="display:none">Ein Liebesbrief erreicht den Romancier und Lebemann R. an seinem einundvierzigsten Geburtstag – die leidenschaftliche Lebensbeichte einer Frau, deren Lebensmittelpunkt er war.<br /><br />Doch sie ist für ihn nur eine belanglose Geliebte unter vielen geblieben, letztlich eine Unbekannte. »Ich klage Dich nicht an, mein Geliebter, nein, ich klage Dich nicht an«, verspricht sie, und doch stellen ihre glühenden Worten das Leben dieses Mannes, der »nur das Leichte, das Spielende, das Gewichtlose« lieben kann und vor Bindungen zurückscheut aus »Angst, in ein Schicksal einzugreifen«, vollständig in Frage.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1617396715" />
    <a title="Rowena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2990642-rowena"><img alt="Rowena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499471926p2/2990642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1617396715?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rowena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rowena" href="/user/show/2990642-rowena">Rowena</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/8123137-letter-from-an-unknown-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2990642-rowena?shelf=german-lit">german-lit</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1617396715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11669379989436251399"><b>“I will tell you the whole story of my life, and it is a life that truly began only on the day I met you. Before that, there was nothing but murky confusion into which my memory never dipped again, some kind of cellar full of dusty, cobwebbed, sombre objects and people.”</b> - Stefan Zweig, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i><br/><br/>I don’t really understand monomania and it’s very uncomfortable yet fascinating to read about the case in this novella. A famous author reads an anonymous letter addressed to him, the </span>
  <span id="freeText11669379989436251399" style="display:none"><b>“I will tell you the whole story of my life, and it is a life that truly began only on the day I met you. Before that, there was nothing but murky confusion into which my memory never dipped again, some kind of cellar full of dusty, cobwebbed, sombre objects and people.”</b> - Stefan Zweig, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i><br /><br />I don’t really understand monomania and it’s very uncomfortable yet fascinating to read about the case in this novella. A famous author reads an anonymous letter addressed to him, the letter details a young girl falling in love with him and the more we read the more is revealed. The author is hooked and so was I. Zweig is one of the best at the psychological short story and I’m still thinking about this story more than a fortnight after I read it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11669379989436251399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2199709356?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BlackOxford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BlackOxford" href="/user/show/17744555-blackoxford">BlackOxford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/8123137-letter-from-an-unknown-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17744555-blackoxford?shelf=german-language">german-language</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2199709356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12834619601055019038"><b>Passive-Aggressive Revenge?</b><br/><br/>Other than as a practice-piece, it is difficult for he to understand much about this short story. A woman obsessed since puberty by a neighbour she has hardly spoken to spends her entire life in a world of fantastic projection. Despite her rescue from poverty, loving family, and opportunities to get on in life, she prefers to senselessly pine over a man to whom she refuses even to give her name. A casual affair, from his side, results in a pregnancy about which she ref</span>
  <span id="freeText12834619601055019038" style="display:none"><b>Passive-Aggressive Revenge?</b><br /><br />Other than as a practice-piece, it is difficult for he to understand much about this short story. A woman obsessed since puberty by a neighbour she has hardly spoken to spends her entire life in a world of fantastic projection. Despite her rescue from poverty, loving family, and opportunities to get on in life, she prefers to senselessly pine over a man to whom she refuses even to give her name. A casual affair, from his side, results in a pregnancy about which she refuses to inform him. Their offspring dies as a young man from unknown causes. She apparently also dies from grief.<br /><br />She has written a letter to him to be delivered post-mortem. The constant refrain of her letter is <i>“Beloved, I am not blaming you. I do not wish to intrude my sorrows into your joyful life.”</i> Yet this is what she has done - maliciously, unrecoverably, and clearly intentionally. Why? Did Zweig believe that a woman, any woman, all women could be psychotic enough to carry out such a programme? Could it be that the story itself is a sort of passive-aggressive revenge by Zweig? If not, his point escapes me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12834619601055019038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3848078977807646136"><b>Stefan Zweig – Letter From An Unknown Woman</b><br/><br/>So much more than a love letter. Not just an unrequited love, but the love felt by the lesser for the more. The kind of love which, if it doesn’t bloom, it kills and gets killed, ending up in a Waterloo that only big ideas can cause. If it does bloom, however, it’s what I believe to be the most meaningful kind of love and the one that, strange as it may seem in its contradiction, can lead to self-awareness and respect. <br/><br/>So many things to be felt in such </span>
  <span id="freeText3848078977807646136" style="display:none"><b>Stefan Zweig – Letter From An Unknown Woman</b><br /><br />So much more than a love letter. Not just an unrequited love, but the love felt by the lesser for the more. The kind of love which, if it doesn’t bloom, it kills and gets killed, ending up in a Waterloo that only big ideas can cause. If it does bloom, however, it’s what I believe to be the most meaningful kind of love and the one that, strange as it may seem in its contradiction, can lead to self-awareness and respect. <br /><br />So many things to be felt in such few pages. An accomplishment that only Zweig could achieve.<br />Brilliant.<br /></span>

<div id="review_3529885629" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3529885629" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2967061-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577653837p2/2967061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3529885629?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/2967061-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/8123137-letter-from-an-unknown-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=banned-books">banned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=novellas-and-short-stories">novellas-and-short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=austria">austria</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2967061-anne?shelf=tragedy">tragedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3529885629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17496584484900170580">This is a dramatic and tragic novella written in the form of a letter from a woman to the man whom she has loved for many years. Stefan Zweig has an amazing ability to understand the human psyche and to write in succinct yet beautiful and impassioned prose. As a reader/listener I was completely drawn in to this story, rapt with attention from beginning to end, feeling the drama as it unfolds more and more strongly. The rhythm of this novella felt like a piece of music with certain phrases repeat</span>
  <span id="freeText17496584484900170580" style="display:none">This is a dramatic and tragic novella written in the form of a letter from a woman to the man whom she has loved for many years. Stefan Zweig has an amazing ability to understand the human psyche and to write in succinct yet beautiful and impassioned prose. As a reader/listener I was completely drawn in to this story, rapt with attention from beginning to end, feeling the drama as it unfolds more and more strongly. The rhythm of this novella felt like a piece of music with certain phrases repeating every so often and after each phrase repetition more of the story is told, building ever higher and higher emotions until the tragic story slows down and ends..<br /><br /> I felt the pain and the passion of this woman who first meets the object of her obsession at the tender age of 13 when he moved into her apartment building. They never met but she watched him as much as possible and was heartbroken when forced to move away with her parents. She remains obsessed with him all of her life. She has only a few encounters with him as an adult woman though each time they meet by chance he never remembers her. This is the bare outline of the story. Further details would only spoil the story.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17496584484900170580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3081042878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3081042878" />
    <a title="Steven Godin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26706841-steven-godin"><img alt="Steven Godin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605181037p2/26706841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3081042878?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Godin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Godin" href="/user/show/26706841-steven-godin">Steven Godin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782081226579" href="/book/show/28929159-lettre-d-une-inconnue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26706841-steven-godin?shelf=classic-fiction">classic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26706841-steven-godin?shelf=austria">austria</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3081042878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9242684813659171601">Letter From an Unknown Woman I found to be a superb piece of writing. This is in my opinion Zweig at his absolute best in terms of stirring something in the reader, even though it starts along familiar, even slightly tedious lines. A girl has a crush on the man across the hall, a handsome, fastidious, famous writer who lives alone with his elderly servant and comes home with elegant women. She gazes at him with a fluttering heart through the spy-hole in her parents front door and sometimes loite</span>
  <span id="freeText9242684813659171601" style="display:none">Letter From an Unknown Woman I found to be a superb piece of writing. This is in my opinion Zweig at his absolute best in terms of stirring something in the reader, even though it starts along familiar, even slightly tedious lines. A girl has a crush on the man across the hall, a handsome, fastidious, famous writer who lives alone with his elderly servant and comes home with elegant women. She gazes at him with a fluttering heart through the spy-hole in her parents front door and sometimes loiters outside hoping for a momentary view of her beloved. When she is old enough she starts work in a shop and continues to stalk him.<br /><br />As an eighteen year-old he one day stops her in the street, as she is very pretty, and doesn’t realize it's the same little neighbour from across the hall, as he never remembers anything that might intrude on his total self-regard. After inviting her to a meal they share a few nights of passion, before he forgets her. She has a child, he has no idea. <br />She sells herself, to rich men as a means to escape poverty, and has many marriage proposals.<br />Then one night her beloved sees her dining in a restaurant with one of her clientele, and again as before he has little idea who she is. After another night together she never hears from him again. <br />After tragedy strikes, she is in a very dark place, and this leads us to the letter she would write him.<br />He is stirred by a faint memory, like a piece of familiar music playing in the distance of a forgotten dream.<br /><br />With much heartbreak, Zweig simply writes of a lovesick heart, resulting in one of the most emotive stories I've read. It lingered around for days in my head, and I was genuinely moved by it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9242684813659171601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5453081918172889833">I bought it yesterday and read it all in about two hours total. I was so moved, I understood so well this woman that loved in the shadows a man that honestly couldn't love anyone... it was heartbreaking, but also representative of what the women I know, myself included, are capable of doing for a great love.   <span id="freeText5453081918172889833" style="display:none">I bought it yesterday and read it all in about two hours total. I was so moved, I understood so well this woman that loved in the shadows a man that honestly couldn't love anyone... it was heartbreaking, but also representative of what the women I know, myself included, are capable of doing for a great love. And the silence that echoes on the other side... Men.<br /><br />We must not forget that it was a man who wrote it, so he was both conscient of the enduring power of a woman's affection, but also of how, not rarely, men despise it.<br />_________________________________<br /><br />Comprei-o ontem e li-o em duas horas. Fiquei tão comovida, entendi tão bem esta mulher que amou nas sombras um homem que, honestamente, não podia amar ninguém... foi desconcertante, mas também representativo das mulheres que conheço, eu incluída, capazes de qualquer coisa por um amor maior. E o silêncio que ecoa do outro lado... Homens.<br /><br />Devemos esquecer-nos de que foi um homem que o escreveu, e que estava, assim, simultaneamente consciente do poder da afeição de uma mulher, mas também, não raramente, desprezam-no.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24456813-letter-from-an-unknown-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=short">short</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/632247-chrissie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2109443689" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16280754302883060150">There is something in us that is attracted to passionate love. Unrequited love pulls not only on the magnetism of passion but also the devastation felt when love is not returned. I am a realist, but I was drawn in too.<br/><br/>This book is to be read with your emotions and your heart. With clinical analysis, it falls apart. It is for this reason I am not going to analyze the story. All you need to know is that the setting is Vienna in the late 1800s.<br/> <br/>The audiobook I listened to was produced by Sonic Movi</span>
  <span id="freeText16280754302883060150" style="display:none">There is something in us that is attracted to passionate love. Unrequited love pulls not only on the magnetism of passion but also the devastation felt when love is not returned. I am a realist, but I was drawn in too.<br /><br />This book is to be read with your emotions and your heart. With clinical analysis, it falls apart. It is for this reason I am not going to analyze the story. All you need to know is that the setting is Vienna in the late 1800s.<br /> <br />The audiobook I listened to was produced by Sonic Movies. I do not like dramatization in the reading of books, but this was what was available to me. Dramatization leaves little left to imagine. The two performing artists who narrate are Heather Wood and K. Anderson Yancy. The reading was alternately too slow and too fast. Doors slam, screams are heard and background music is added. None of this is to my taste. <br /><br />I have given the audio performance one star. I have given the author’s lines three. Being the realist that I am and the total lack of credibility of the story, I should logically not have liked this, but I did.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2282796007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282796007" />
    <a title="Rym " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68309582-rym"><img alt="Rym " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598825122p2/68309582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2282796007?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rym " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rym " href="/user/show/68309582-rym">Rym </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782234063112" href="/book/show/6427100-lettre-d-une-inconnue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282796007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11407461276733985398"><blockquote>
  <i>“I will tell you the whole story of my life, and it is a life that truly began only on the day I met you. Before that, there was nothing but murky confusion into which my memory never dipped again, some kind of cellar full of dusty, cobwebbed, sombre objects and people.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1546174.Letter_from_an_Unknown_Woman' title='Letter from an Unknown Woman by Karen Hollinger' rel='nofollow noopener'>Letter from an Unknown Woman</a> <i>(German: Brief einer Unbekannten)</i> is a novella written by the Austrian writer <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig' title='Stefan Zweig' rel='nofollow noopener'> Stefan Zweig</a> —and published in 1922.<br/><br/>On his birthday, a renowned author – referred to as R. — receives a letter from a</span>
  <span id="freeText11407461276733985398" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“I will tell you the whole story of my life, and it is a life that truly began only on the day I met you. Before that, there was nothing but murky confusion into which my memory never dipped again, some kind of cellar full of dusty, cobwebbed, sombre objects and people.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1546174.Letter_from_an_Unknown_Woman" title="Letter from an Unknown Woman by Karen Hollinger" rel="nofollow noopener">Letter from an Unknown Woman</a> <i>(German: Brief einer Unbekannten)</i> is a novella written by the Austrian writer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig" title="Stefan Zweig" rel="nofollow noopener"> Stefan Zweig</a> —and published in 1922.<br /><br />On his birthday, a renowned author – referred to as R. — receives a letter from an unknown woman. In which this latter gives a detailed account of her life to the writer. <br /> As a teenager, the woman had lived in poverty with her widowed mother in the same building as R.—and had fallen in love with him as soon as she saw him. Despite the circumstances <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(she leaves Vienna —and moves to Innsbruck when her mother remarries) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, her love for the handsome author, remains ‘unblemished’. Sadly, the poor woman will find herself engulfed in the flames of this poisonous passion.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1546174.Letter_from_an_Unknown_Woman" title="Letter from an Unknown Woman by Karen Hollinger" rel="nofollow noopener"> Letter from an Unknown Woman</a> has multiple levels of meaning. Whenever I read classics, I tend to go beyond the literal meaning —and to interpret the different aspects of a literary work in reference to its historical background as well as the author’s life. This time, however, I will try to just relish this story in and of itself. <br /><br />To be candid, I was moved to tears by this short story. Despite the fact that it was a pretty ordinary story and that the major plot twist was utterly predictable, it was nigh-on impossible for me not to weep. What rendered this short story so heart-wrenching was not the theme of unrequited love, but rather the poignant portrayal of the loss of dignity —and the objectification of the individual (women in this case). It is through the character of the mysterious woman that Zweig introduces us to both human frailty —and irrationality in relation to love. The woman was driven by her impulses —and ended up losing herself in the process of loving her neighbour. <br />She became a slave to her own emotions —and <i>une fille de joie devouée</i> , in the name of love. Unfortunately, her tremendous efforts to be noticed —and acknowledged by the young author were in vain, as this latter only perceived her as a mere courtesan, one nameless woman among many others that he ditched as soon as his ‘needs’ were satisfied.<br />However, this did not prevent the anonymous woman to devote herself to him —and to love him with (as she describes it in her letter) <i>“such doglike fidelity”.</i><br />What R. deemed to be a one-night stand, was for his beautiful courtesan a dream come true; she could feel him lying next to her, inhale his smell —and ‘own’ him for once in her life. Her desperation to be part of his life —and be loved back was literally heartbreaking. Losing one’s <i>amour-propre</i> while trying to gain someone else’s love is probably one of the worst feelings that a person can experience. Love is sometimes too costly; it drains your energy, it takes away your independance, your time —and so many other valuable things. <br /><br />Love is an investment, but when it is unrequited, it becomes problematic. This investment becomes destructive..it consumes you, it weakens you —and you end up losing all the self-respect that you had. You lose your own identity —and your <i>joie de vivre</i>, because your world has been revolving around that single person for so long that you ended up forgetting how to carry on living without them.. You find yourself disorientated..lost in the middle of nowhere..<br />The mysterious woman gave the best of her to the young author. She sacrificed her dignity, her body —and her energy for someone who failed to appreciate her real value. This infatuation with R. restrained her from moving on —and living for her own sake. All of her actions were directed by her desire to be part of this latter’s life. If she hadn’t allowed her heart to control her <i>moindres faits et gestes</i>, she would have probably led a happier life. Unfortunately, our character did not live; she survived..counting the days, the months —and the years. The saddest part is that the woman’s love for the author exceeded her love for herself to the point that —even on her deathbed— her last thoughts were all devoted to her eternal love. <br /><br />An old friend of mine once told me that <i>“love without reason cannot survive”</i>. To be honest, I did not get what he meant at that time, because I believed that <b>TRUE love</b> somehow involved irrationality. I thought that true love required us to follow our hearts rather than our minds, but now I guess I understood what he wanted to tell me. There should be a balance between the mind —and the heart. Loving someone does not mean that you have to stop using your mind —and turn into an irrational being. This can turn into madness..you should not allow your emotions to control you as you could end up harming yourself and/or the person you love. You can love someone with all your heart, but still be wise —and mature. You can love someone unconditionally, but still make the right choices —and choose the right path. True love is not about suppressing reason; it is rather about combining the two in order to avoid the annihilation of any of them. You can deeply love someone, but then realize that you made them suffocate by invading their personal space. You should never LIVE solely for someone even if you love them with all your heart.. keep some love for yourself..know your limits —and respect theirs. If someone is meant to be yours, they will gravitate towards you..if not, then it was simply not meant to be. Learn to love yourself first before loving someone else —and investing into a relationship, because if you don’t love yourself, <i>then how can you expect another person to love you the way you deserve to be loved, to respect you —and to stand by you?</i> It all starts with you. Give yourself the time to heal from the things that have hurt you, to embrace your imperfections —and mostly don’t rush. Some wounds need more time to heal than others. Most importantly, never do something that contradicts your principles for anyone as you will be filled with remorse. Stay faithful to yourself —and to your convictions.<br /><br />Apart from the theme of unrequited love —and the things that go along with it, Zweig also lambasted health care institutions. He portrayed the inhumanity —and the barbarity with which patients were treated. I’m not sure whether it is the case —or not, yet I somehow felt that Zweig had kind of a feminist standpoint. His description of the events did not seem impartial as he was somehow depicting the constraints imposed on women within the society. In fact, it appeared as if Stefan Zweig was trying to highlight the struggles faced by women —and the prejudices to which they are exposed on a daily basis. This short story gives you the impression that being a woman is somehow a curse in the sense that society is so judgmental towards ‘females’ that sometimes being a woman becomes so overwhelming. Anyway, as I said, this short story can be interpreted in various manners, but I simply wanted to focus on the above-mentioned points rather than dig deeper.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Quotes:</b>
</u><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“All I know is that I shall be alone again. There is nothing more terrible than to be alone among human beings.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Now all I have in the world is you, you who know nothing about me, you who are now amusing yourself without a care in the world, dallying with things and with people. I have only you, who never knew me, and whom I have always loved.”</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="11407461276733985398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="George" class="user" itemprop="url" name="George" href="/user/show/12187924-george">George</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 960283174X" href="/book/show/12107390">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

  <span id="freeText12189791561503413606" style="display:none">4.5 Read as part of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17329076.Letter_from_an_Unknown_Woman_and_Other_Stories" title="Letter from an Unknown Woman and Other Stories by Stefan Zweig" rel="nofollow noopener">Letter from an Unknown Woman and Other Stories</a>.<br /><br />The beautiful tragedy of feverish longing and unrequited love captured in Zweig's rich prose, that I loved so much already in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2376087.The_Post_Office_Girl" title="The Post-Office Girl by Stefan Zweig" rel="nofollow noopener">The Post-Office Girl</a>. And how fitting that Cigarettes After Sex' version of "Keep on loving you" came on the moment I started reading. I will forgive the heroine her penchant for melodrama, because it's slightly embarrassing to recall it in great detail today, but my two decades old diaries are the proof that I've "been there, done that".<br /><br />"I loved you from that second on. I know that women have often said those words to you, spoilt as you are. But believe me, no one ever loved you as slavishly, with such dog-like devotion, as the creature I was then and have always remained, for there is nothing on earth like the love of a child that passes unnoticed in the dark because she has no hope: her love is so submissive, so much a servant's love, passionately and lying in wait, in a way that the avid yet unconsciously demanding love of a grown woman can never be."</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer971863806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7291889288913588793"><i>To the one who never knew me,<br/> I miss you so much today,much more than I have felt in many days.. I feel tired,sick.. I feel my legs go weak.. I think I should go to bed.. But how can i go to bed without sharing my thoughts with you.. So,like always,I sit near my table with my table-lamp on,writing to you.. <br/><br/> You didn't ask me why it is that I miss you especially today.. You never ask anything..! I happened to read a book today,much like a long story.. It was about a man receiving letter from an u</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7291889288913588793" style="display:none"><i>To the one who never knew me,<br /> I miss you so much today,much more than I have felt in many days.. I feel tired,sick.. I feel my legs go weak.. I think I should go to bed.. But how can i go to bed without sharing my thoughts with you.. So,like always,I sit near my table with my table-lamp on,writing to you.. <br /><br /> You didn't ask me why it is that I miss you especially today.. You never ask anything..! I happened to read a book today,much like a long story.. It was about a man receiving letter from an unknown woman on his birthday.. She tells him how long she had waited for him to see her,to recognize her.. She tells him how she spent her whole life waiting.. It hurt much,to see her pain.. To see being unrecognized all her life,by the one she considers her life. I saw myself in her.. It's really painful,when you fail to see me even when I'm in front of you.. You're always leaving,somewhere or another.. You always promise to come back,you always promise 'tomorrow',but tomorrow never arrives.. Like the white roses gifted by that girl,my life remains in a vase as an unwanted gift,one that you never notice.. I've become like those books in your shelves which you never even dust.. I wonder how that author wrote it.. He never knew me.. <br /><br /> I'm becoming much attracted towards his books.. He hurts me with his words,and hurt reminds me of you.. Pain is the only thing you ever gave me.. <br /><br /> Yet I won't complain,my love.. You are the best thing that ever happened to me.. You made me see the woman in me.. I learned love through you.. And in you,it will end..<br /><br /> I've drunk five glasses of water since I started writing this.. I'm feeling more thirsty.. I was shivering by the time I reached the end of that book.. I feel heaviness in my head,on my eyes.. I think I should go to bed.. I'll see you in my dreams.. Will you see me at least then.?!!<br /><br />Forever yours only<br />....</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7291889288913588793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9547953777962238304">My first Stefan Zweig. I was uncomfortable with a male writer portraying a fictional young woman's obsessive love for a male writer, a love that bordered on monomania. But I stuck with this little novella until the end, and found it to be an incisive indictment of the male gaze, what it misses and inflicts.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1038763466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038763466" />
    <a title="Czarny Pies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies"><img alt="Czarny Pies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400687408p2/29160274.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038763466?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Czarny Pies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Czarny Pies" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies">Czarny Pies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782234063112" href="/book/show/6427100-lettre-d-une-inconnue">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone unfamiliar with the work of Stefan Zweig</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Czarny by: </span>
      Lucie Novak
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29160274-czarny-pies?shelf=german-lit">german-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038763466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10629273092073858616">This novel takes form of monologue in which a character recounts a story berating the listener for past sins of omission and commission. This device can be effective the first time that one encounters it. It powefuly represents the intense emotion of the protagonist and maintains a high level of tension through-out the piece. I first encountered this form in the one act opera of La voix humaine (musique Francois Poulenc, livret Jean Cocteau). I have also encountered it in Strindberg's Stronger, </span>
  <span id="freeText10629273092073858616" style="display:none">This novel takes form of monologue in which a character recounts a story berating the listener for past sins of omission and commission. This device can be effective the first time that one encounters it. It powefuly represents the intense emotion of the protagonist and maintains a high level of tension through-out the piece. I first encountered this form in the one act opera of La voix humaine (musique Francois Poulenc, livret Jean Cocteau). I have also encountered it in Strindberg's Stronger, Sandor Marai's Embers, Sandor Marai's Metamorpheses of a Marriage and Bergman's Personna. I do not who in fact first devised the technique. In any event, having finished La Lettre d'une Inconnue, I had am now highly jaded and will make every effort to ensure that I do not read another work in the school.<br /><br />For person who is fresh to format, La lettre d'une inconnue must be a stunning tour de force. A letter arrives at the home of the author's alter ego in which the writer announces that she is a former lover that he does not remember. Moreover, she is the mother of his child who has just died in the great epidemic of Spanish Influenza. She then goes through the appalling story of her life spent in unrequited love for the reader. She was a poor neighbour who loved him but was always ignored. Several years later, she encounters him in the street and they have a three day romance in which the child is conceived. They have another one-night stand several years later in which again he does not recognize her. He simply pays her the standard fee for a prostitute. As the letter closes, the woman announces that she too is dying from the Spanish influenza and will be dead at the time he reads the letter.<br /><br />My experience with Stefan Zweig is that he always sends the reader to skate on thin ice covering a lake in the form of bottomless meldorama. Sometimes, the ice cracks drowning the reader in bathos. With la lettre d'une inconnu the reader lands all his triple lutzes and axels and skates off the ice intact.<br /><br />La lettre d'une inconnue will be a good read for anyone who has seen a friend become trapped in unrequited love and fail to escape. It will be an absolutely powerful work for anyone who has remained obsessed for several years with a person who does not return his or her love.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10629273092073858616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3042771177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3042771177" />
    <a title="Caro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2344161-caro"><img alt="Caro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301834766p2/2344161.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3042771177?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caro" href="/user/show/2344161-caro">Caro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3042771177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2190154382269318822">Phenomenal writing but I just can't love it. <br/><br/>Stefan Zweig, in this short and concise Viennese novella, invented the invisible woman, the doormat, the biblical female idiot, the forgotten woman, the discarted, slavish 500s concubine in some wild harem.<br/><br/>I'm pretty sure no woman literary or otherwise, ever doormatted so hard before Stefan Zweig's writer protagonist playboy with early romantic Alzheimers received a letter from some woman whose child just died. <br/><br/>The story, if you can call it that, was </span>
  <span id="freeText2190154382269318822" style="display:none">Phenomenal writing but I just can't love it. <br /><br />Stefan Zweig, in this short and concise Viennese novella, invented the invisible woman, the doormat, the biblical female idiot, the forgotten woman, the discarted, slavish 500s concubine in some wild harem.<br /><br />I'm pretty sure no woman literary or otherwise, ever doormatted so hard before Stefan Zweig's writer protagonist playboy with early romantic Alzheimers received a letter from some woman whose child just died. <br /><br />The story, if you can call it that, was full of anachronisms. The writer, who absolutely could not have been anything but male, is almost certainly the less mondaine, less observant, less talented than the woman who wrote a letter to him. The letter that fills 90% of the whole novella, is written with resolute drive, impeccable restraint and a stunning knowledge of using repitions, metaphores and images instead of descriptions. The Woman is as such superior to the male writer to whom she writes.<br /><br />She is also superior in a social capacity. Her many friends, nothing to her, are intelligent, kind people, rich and warm. The Woman is loved and adored, cherished and coddled inspite of her one dalliance.<br /><br />Yet the Male, the writer, is so above the woman in the whole narrative. He remains, in the perspective of the letter, an aloof person, a demigod. It is ironic that the one person who understands him completely is unknown to him, and as she dies, there is no more understanding for his antisocial, pathetic lifestyle from anyone. There is no substance to him except in her. He is, so ironically, within his superiority, depending on the approval and appraisal of a woman, unable to subsist on his own. <br /><br />In the end, the Woman wins. Slavish as she was in her lifetime, she enslaves, in her death, the one person she never wished to beg for attention. It is very nearly, a tale of revenge.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2190154382269318822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer9569238426323680272">so I spent like an hour earlier trying to find this book on here constantly coming up with 24 hours in the life of a woman, and right before giving up and assuming there were two titles I wiki'd and learned those are two different (if seemingly similarly themed) books. so first I pulled the letter from an unknown woman isbn off of the other book where it was located on goodreads. then I searched again and finally found the book. This is called a novella, but at best it's a short story and one th</span>
  <span id="freeText9569238426323680272" style="display:none">so I spent like an hour earlier trying to find this book on here constantly coming up with 24 hours in the life of a woman, and right before giving up and assuming there were two titles I wiki'd and learned those are two different (if seemingly similarly themed) books. so first I pulled the letter from an unknown woman isbn off of the other book where it was located on goodreads. then I searched again and finally found the book. This is called a novella, but at best it's a short story and one that is basically impossible to find. I tried to figure out what book it was inside and couldn't, so I found the text online and read it on my computer. <br /><br />this was recommended to me by that stalker book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/688421.Unrequited_Love_On_Stalking_and_Being_Stalked_a_story_of_obsessive_passion" title="Unrequited Love On Stalking and Being Stalked a story of obsessive passion by Gregory Dart" rel="nofollow noopener">Unrequited Love: On Stalking and Being Stalked a story of obsessive passion</a>) I just read as an example of a stalker, and it is. <br /><br />I got this email once from a guy that said, paraphrase "I think we went out before once and we didn't really have a chance to get to know each other so I thought we could again". Well I said yes and I met up with him. From this experience I learned: 1. there was a reason I'd never gone out with him again, I didn't like him. 2. I had no idea who the fuck he was or if we'd actually ever met, he insisted we had. That is kind of what this book is about without the informing of previous meetings. <br /><br />It's sad, cause zweig was sad. <br /><br />more importantly at the beginning of the version I read it was stated: <br /><br /><i>During the years at Salzburg, Zweig began to suspect that Hitler's persecution of Jews was directed at him personally, and he never recovered from this paranoia. </i><br /><br />what's not to love. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LplSzw/hC275wBYZJENfVsS8d9z5FAh2Vni1+BsVO1214Tqp5cr+qNBc3HyXq9uZTwOvAe1dbyJqLzKKuVmgow==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TMtw7Sq9fNUsWdPv8l2Z6PYsohNqGlMh4M9HBtgmadTXsxiLwJaJEwXFGYpBtR0nfZN6zn5TNHXcmMB0emryKg==')})
  }
//]]>

Birçok <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText416039786869526154\" style=\"display:none\">Peyami Safa\'nın şaheserlerinden Dokuzuncu Hariciye Koğuşu, Türk edebiyatında &quot;insan ruhunun derinliklerinde ve labirentlerinde dolaşan ilk roman&quot; olması ve hasta bir insanı ve onun psikolojisini ele alması bakımından önemli bir yere sahiptir. Birçok araştırmacı ve yazar tarafından Türk edebiyatında bir ilk kabul edilen Dokuzuncu Hariciye Koğuşu, Tanpınar\'ın dediği gibi, &quot;acının ve ıstırabın yegâne kitabı&quot; olarak hem kemiyet hem de keyfiyet bakımından başka hiçbir eser olmasa da Türk romanının var olduğuna delil gösterilebilecek kudrette bir eserdir. İlber Hoca bu kitapta, bir insanın, çocukluktan itibaren hayatın hemen her alanında ihtiyaç duyacağı çözümleri nasıl bulabileceğini örnekler vererek anlatıyor. “Herkes kendi talihinin mimarıdır” sözünü hatırlatarak, kendi yolunu çizmenin ne anlama geldiğini tüm kritik noktalarıyla yorumluyor.\n\nBir ömrü hakkıyla yaşayabilmek ve yaşanan her andan tat alabilmek için önce ne lazımdır? \n\nİnsan hayatı kaç dönemden oluşur ve her bir dönemde neleri tecrübe etmek gerekir? \n\n15, 25, 40 ve 55 yaşları neden birer eşiktir?\n\nİnsan kimden, ne öğrenebilir? \n\nKendi kendini yetiştirmek nasıl mümkün olur? \n\nKişi mesleğini neye göre seçmelidir?\n\nBir işin uzmanı olmak ve o uzmanlık bilgisiyle çalışmak için nelere ihtiyaç vardır? \n\nBir dil, en iyi nasıl ve ne zaman öğrenilir? \n\nEn verimli sonucu alabilmek için nasıl çalışmak gerekir?\n\nSorumluluk sahibi bir insan, kendisi veya çocukları için nasıl bir eğitim modeli aramalıdır?\n\nHayata değer katmak için ne tür insanları arayıp bulmak gerekir? \n\nDoğru kararları alabilmek için en çok kimleri dinlemek gerekir? \n\nEn iyi nasıl seyahat edilir; bir şehir nasıl dolaşılır?\n\nHangi müze, hangi meydan, hangi sokakları görmek için dünyanın bir ucuna kadar gidilebilir?\n\nİyi film, güzel müzik, doğru kitap nedir? \n\nHangi temel eserleri dinlemeli, okumalı ve seyretmeliyiz?\n\nİnsan yaşadığı şehirden tam manasıyla nasıl yararlanabilir?\n\n“Bir Ömür Nasıl Yaşanır?”, ülkemizin medarıiftiharı olmuş bir tarihçinin gözünden, insanın hayattaki anlam arayışına, bu arayışın tadını nasıl çıkaracağına ve süreç boyunca       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig">About Stefan Zweig</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/25573.Stefan_Zweig"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1190140738p3/25573.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5177840795508861425">Stefan Zweig was one of the world's most famous writers during the 1920s and 1930s, especially in the U.S., South America, and Europe. He produced novels, plays, biographies, and journalist pieces. Among his most famous works are <i>Beware of Pity</i>, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i>, and <i>Mary, Queen of Scotland and the Isles</i>. He and his second wife committed suicide in 1942.<br/><br/>Zweig studied in Austria, France</span>
  <span id="freeText5177840795508861425" style="display:none">Stefan Zweig was one of the world's most famous writers during the 1920s and 1930s, especially in the U.S., South America, and Europe. He produced novels, plays, biographies, and journalist pieces. Among his most famous works are <i>Beware of Pity</i>, <i>Letter from an Unknown Woman</i>, and <i>Mary, Queen of Scotland and the Isles</i>. He and his second wife committed suicide in 1942.<br /><br />Zweig studied in Austria, France, and Germany before settling in Salzburg in 1913. In 1934, driven into exile by the Nazis, he emigrated to England and then, in 1940, to Brazil by way of New York. Finding only growing loneliness and disillusionment in their new surroundings, he and his second wife committed suicide.<br /><br />Zweig's interest in psychology and the teachings of Sigmund Freud led to his most characteristic work, the subtle portrayal of character. Zweig's essays include studies of Honoré de Balzac, Charles Dickens, and Fyodor Dostoyevsky (<i>Drei Meister</i>, 1920; <i>Three Masters</i>) and of Friedrich Hölderlin, Heinrich von Kleist, and Friedrich Nietzsche (<i>Der Kampf mit dem Dämon</i>, 1925; <i>Master Builders</i>). He achieved popularity with <i>Sternstunden der Menschheit</i> (1928; <i>The Tide of Fortune</i>), five historical portraits in miniature. He wrote full-scale, intuitive rather than objective, biographies of the French statesman Joseph Fouché (1929), Mary Stuart (1935), and others. His stories include those in <i>Verwirrung der Gefühle</i> (1925; <i>Conflicts</i>). He also wrote a psychological novel, <i>Ungeduld des Herzens</i> (1938; <i>Beware of Pity</i>), and translated works of Charles Baudelaire, Paul Verlaine, and Emile Verhaeren.<br /><br />Most recently, his works provided the inspiration for 2014 film <i>The Grand Budapest Hotel</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5177840795508861425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
